{"code":["var model = function() {\n\n    var fair = flip()\n    var p_heads = fair ? 0.5 : 0.85\n    var flip1 = flip(p_heads) ? 'H' : 'T'\n    var flip2 = flip(p_heads) ? 'H' : 'T'\n\n    condition(flip1 == 'T' && flip2 == 'T')\n    fair\n\n}\nvar dist = Infer({method:'enumerate'}, model)\n\nviz(dist, {xLabel: 'Fair', yLabel: 'P(Fair | T,T)'})\nprint(\"P(Fair=True  | Flip1=Tails, Flip2=Tails) = \" + Math.exp(dist.score(true)))\n\n// Note: dist.score returns a log probability, which is why need Math.exp","var makeModel = function(f) {return function() {\n    var fair = flip()\n    var p_heads = fair ? 0.5 : 0.85\n    var flip1 = flip(p_heads) ? 'H' : 'T'\n    var flip2 = flip(p_heads) ? (isEasy ? 0.9 : 0.8) : (isEasy ? 0.55 : 0.25);\n            return flip(passProb);\n        };\n        \n        // Pass the memoized functions to f for further usage\n        f(studyHabit, examDifficulty, passExam);\n    };\n};\n\neditor.put(\"makeModel\", makeModel)","var makeModel = editor.get(\"makeModel\")\n\n// Inference\nvar dist = Infer({method: 'enumerate'}, true);\n    \n    return studyHabit('student');\n}));\n\n// Visualize the results\nviz(dist);\n\n// Calculate the probability\nprint(\"The probability that a student who passed an exam also studied is     var studyHabit = mem(function(student) {\n            return flip(0.9);  // 90% chance the student is studying\n        });\n        \n        // Memoized function for exam difficulty\n        var examDifficulty = mem(function(exam) {\n            return flip(0.15);  // 15% chance the exam is easy\n        });\n        \n        // Function to calculate passing the exam\n        var passExam = hard rather than easy. Consequently, the updated model would generally show a higher probability for the \"hard\" category for Exam 1, as the collective failure rate becomes less likely under the assumption that the exam was easy.","if multiple students are failing the exams, it is more likely that these students are not studying rather than the exams being difficult. This would indeed make it more probable that the exams are easy and, in turn, decrease the probability that Student 1 is a studier.","The new information that Student 1 has passed Exam 3 and Exam 4 increases the likelihood that Student 1 is a studier. Consequently, the failure of Student 1 in Exam 1 and Exam 2 makes it more plausible that those exams were hard, thereby reducing the probability that Exam 1 is easy.","my subject's answer\n(b) Student 1 is a studier: Down Exam 1 is easy: Up\n(c) Student 1 is a studier: Down Exam 1 is easy: Up\n(d) Student 1 is a studier: No change Exam 1 is easy: Up\n(e) Student 1 is a studier: Up Exam 1 is easy: Up\n\nmy network's answer\n(b) Student 1 is a studier: Down Exam 1 is easy: Up\n(c) Student 1 is a studier: Up Exam 1 is easy: Down\n(d) Student 1 is a studier: Down Exam 1 is easy: Up\n(e) Student 1 is a studier: Up Exam 1 is easy: Down","Changing the priors can influence the strength of the \"explaining away\" effect, where the observation of one variable can reduce the need for another variable to explain the observed data. If the new priors make studying or exam difficulty more or less likely a priori, this could either amplify or attenuate the extent to which evidence for one variable \"explains away\" the need for the other to be true.","As new information was introduced, specifically the performance of multiple students across multiple exams, the posterior probabilities concerning the instructor's leniency and the course's level of advancement likely became more focused. The added data provides more evidence, refining the model's estimates and reducing uncertainty about these parameters.","By replacing the `flip` function with a `beta` distribution, I transitioned the study habits from being a discrete random variable to a continuous one. This allows for a more nuanced representation of students' study habits. The use of the `beta` distribution necessitates the employment of alternative inference methods suitable for continuous variables, such as MCMC, as \"enumerate\" is not applicable. The modification adds complexity to the model but also enhances its potential accuracy in addressing questions related to study habits and exam outcomes.",""],"savedAt":"10/27/2023 11:52:37 PM"}
